<th scope="row" style="font-weight:normal;"><a href="/wiki/Guangdong_Romanization#Hakka" title="Guangdong Romanization">Romanization</a></th>
<td>vu<sup>24</sup> lu<sup>24</sup> mug<sup>2</sup> ce<sup>11</sup> qid<sup>2</sup> · ng<sup>31</sup> pau<sup>55</sup> lid<sup>5</sup> sii<sup>55</sup> kien<sup>55</sup></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;background-color: #dcffc9;"><a href="/wiki/Cantonese" title="Cantonese">Yue: Cantonese</a></th>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row" style="font-weight:normal;"><a href="/wiki/Jyutping" title="Jyutping">Jyutping</a></th>
<td>wu<sup>1</sup> lou<sup>5</sup> muk<sup>6</sup> cai<sup>4</sup> ng<sup>5</sup> bou<sup>6</sup> lik<sup>6</sup> si<sup>6</sup> gin<sup>6*2</sup></td>

<tr>
<th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;background-color: #dcffc9;"><a href="/wiki/Southern_Min" title="Southern Min">Southern Min</a></th>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row" style="font-weight:normal;"><a href="/wiki/Hokkien" title="Hokkien">Hokkien</a> <a href="/wiki/Pe%CC%8Dh-%C5%8De-j%C4%AB" title="Pe̍h-ōe-jī">POJ</a></th>
<td>oo-lóo-bo̍k-tsè tshit-ngóo pō-li̍k sū-kiānn</td>
</tr>
</table>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;background-color: #b0c4de;">Uyghur name</th>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row" style="font-weight:normal;"><a href="/wiki/Uyghur_language" title="Uyghur language">Uyghur</a></th>
<td>
<div style="direction:rtl;">
<div style="text-align:right;"><span lang="ug"><span lang="ug" style="font-size: 135%">بەشىنچى ئىيۇل ۋەقەسى</span><br /></span>
<div style="text-align:left;"><i>Beshinchi iyul weqesi</i><br />
<div style="text-align:left;">"5 July incident"</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>The <b>July 2009 Ürümqi riots</b><sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> were a series of violent riots over several days that broke out on 5 July 2009 in <a href="/wiki/%C3%9Cr%C3%BCmqi" title="Ürümqi">Ürümqi</a>, the capital city of the <a href="/wiki/Xinjiang_Uyghur_Autonomous_Region" class="mw-redirect" title="Xinjiang Uyghur Autonomous Region">Xinjiang Uyghur Autonomous Region</a> (XUAR), in northwestern <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Republic_of_China" class="mw-redirect" title="People's Republic of China">People's Republic of China</a> (PRC). The first day's rioting, which involved at least 1,000 <a href="/wiki/Uyghur_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Uyghur people">Uyghurs</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-bbc_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc-6">[6]</a></sup> began as a protest but escalated into violent attacks that mainly targeted <a href="/wiki/Han_ethnicity" class="mw-redirect" title="Han ethnicity">Han</a> people. <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Armed_Police" title="People's Armed Police">People's Armed Police</a> were deployed, and two days later hundreds of Han people clashed with both police and Uyghurs. PRC officials said that a total of 197 people died, among those killed most of them are Hans,<sup id="cite_ref-Xinhua197_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Xinhua197-2">[2]</a></sup> with 1,721 others injured<sup id="cite_ref-scmp20090717_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-scmp20090717-3">[3]</a></sup> and many vehicles and buildings destroyed; however, Uyghur exile groups say the death toll is higher. Many men disappeared during wide-scale police sweeps in the days following the riots; <a href="/wiki/Human_Rights_Watch" title="Human Rights Watch">Human Rights Watch</a> (HRW) documented 43 cases<sup id="cite_ref-upitt_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-upitt-7">[7]</a></sup> and said figures for real <a href="/wiki/Forced_disappearance" title="Forced disappearance">disappearances</a> were likely to be much higher.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC8317644_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC8317644-8">[8]</a></sup></p>
<p>Rioting began when the police confronted the march calling for a full investigation into the <a href="/wiki/Shaoguan_incident" title="Shaoguan incident">Shaoguan incident</a>, a brawl in southern China several days earlier in which two Uyghurs had been killed.<sup id="cite_ref-nyt090705_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nyt090705-9">[9]</a></sup> However, observers disagree on what caused the protests to become violent. The PRC central government alleged that the riots themselves were planned from abroad by the <a href="/wiki/World_Uyghur_Congress" title="World Uyghur Congress">World Uyghur Congress</a> (WUC) and its leader <a href="/wiki/Rebiya_Kadeer" title="Rebiya Kadeer">Rebiya Kadeer</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-reut090705_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-reut090705-10">[10]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-timesonline_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-timesonline-11">[11]</a></sup> while Kadeer denies fomenting the violence in her fight for Uyghur "self-determination."<sup id="cite_ref-profile050317_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-profile050317-12">[12]</a></sup> Uyghur exile groups claim that the escalation was caused by the police's use of excessive force.<sup id="cite_ref-Timewestwar_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Timewestwar-13">[13]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-afp090706_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-afp090706-14">[14]</a></sup></p>
<p>Chinese media coverage of the Ürümqi riots was extensive, and was compared favourably to that of the <a href="/wiki/2008_Tibetan_unrest" title="2008 Tibetan unrest">unrest in Tibet in 2008</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ft00144_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ft00144-15">[15]</a></sup> When the riots began, communications were immediately cut off. In the weeks that followed, official sources reported that over 1,000 Uyghurs were arrested and detained;<sup id="cite_ref-BBC1500_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC1500-16">[16]</a></sup> Uyghur-run mosques were temporarily closed.<sup id="cite_ref-bbcJ10_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbcJ10-17">[17]</a></sup> The communication limitations<sup id="cite_ref-internetreopen_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-internetreopen-18">[18]</a></sup> and armed police presence remained in place as of January 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-shadows_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-shadows-19">[19]</a></sup> By November&#160;2009, over 400 individuals faced criminal charges for their actions during the riots.<sup id="cite_ref-riotwoman_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-riotwoman-20">[20]</a></sup> Nine were executed in November 2009,<sup id="cite_ref-bbcnov_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbcnov-21">[21]</a></sup> and by February 2010, at least 26 had received death sentences.<sup id="cite_ref-26sentences_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26sentences-22">[22]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Background">Background</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=July_2009_%C3%9Cr%C3%BCmqi_riots&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Background">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Uyghur_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Uyghur people">Uyghur people</a>, <a href="/wiki/History_of_Xinjiang" title="History of Xinjiang">History of Xinjiang</a>, <a href="/wiki/Islamicisation_and_Turkicisation_of_Xinjiang" title="Islamicisation and Turkicisation of Xinjiang">Islamicisation and Turkicisation of Xinjiang</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Migration_to_Xinjiang" title="Migration to Xinjiang">Migration to Xinjiang</a></div>
<p>Xinjiang is a large central-Asian region within the People's Republic of China comprising numerous minority groups: 45% of its population are Uyghurs, and 40% are Han.<sup id="cite_ref-2000census_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2000census-23">[23]</a></sup> Its heavily industrialised capital, Ürümqi, has a population of more than 2.3&#160;million, about 75% of whom are Han, 12.8% are Uyghur, and 10% are from other ethnic groups.<sup id="cite_ref-2000census_23-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2000census-23">[23]</a></sup></p>
<p>In general, Uyghurs and the mostly Han government disagree on which group has greater historical claim to the Xinjiang region: Uyghurs believe their ancestors were indigenous to the area, whereas government policy considers present-day Xinjiang to have belonged to China since around 200&#160;BC.<sup id="cite_ref-Gladney_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gladney-24">[24]</a></sup> According to PRC policy, Uyghurs are classified as a <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_minorities_in_China" title="Ethnic minorities in China">National Minority</a> rather than an indigenous group—in other words, they are considered to be no more indigenous to Xinjiang than the Han, and have no special rights to the land under the law.<sup id="cite_ref-Gladney_24-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gladney-24">[24]</a></sup> The People's Republic has presided over the <a href="/wiki/Migration_to_Xinjiang" title="Migration to Xinjiang">migration into Xinjiang</a> of millions of Han, who dominate the region economically and politically.<sup id="cite_ref-CACI_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CACI-25">[25]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Timeboom_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Timeboom-27">[27]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-winsandloses_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-winsandloses-28">[28]</a></sup></p>
<p>Uyghur nationalists often incorrectly claim that 5% of Xinjiang's population in 1949 was Han, and that the other 95% was Uyghur, erasing the presence of <a href="/wiki/Kazakh_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Kazakh people">Kazakhs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hui_people" title="Hui people">Huis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mongols" title="Mongols">Mongols</a>, <a href="/wiki/Xibe_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Xibe people">Xibes</a> and others, and ignoring the fact that Hans were around one third of Xinjiang's population in 1800, during the time of the <a href="/wiki/Qing_Dynasty" class="mw-redirect" title="Qing Dynasty">Qing Dynasty</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> Professor of Chinese and Central Asian History at Georgetown University, James A. Millward wrote that foreigners often mistakenly think that <a href="/wiki/Urumqi" class="mw-redirect" title="Urumqi">Urumqi</a> was originally a Uyghur city and that the Chinese destroyed its Uyghur character and culture, however, Urumqi was founded as a Chinese city by Han and Hui (Tungans), and it is the Uyghurs who are new to the city.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> While a few people try to give a misportrayal of the historical Qing situation in light of the contemporary situation in Xinjiang with Han migration, and claim that the Qing settlements and state farms were an anti-Uyghur plot to replace them in their land, Professor James A. Millward pointed out that the Qing agricultural colonies in reality had nothing to do with Uyghur and their land, since the Qing banned settlement of Han in the Uyghur Tarim Basin and in fact directed the Han settlers instead to settle in the non-Uyghur Dzungaria and the new city of Urumqi, so that the state farms which were settled with 155,000 Han Chinese from 1760-1830 were all in Dzungaria and Urumqi, where there was only an insignificant amount of Uyghurs, instead of the Tarim Basin oases.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup></p>
<p>At the start of the 19th century, 40 years after the Qing reconquest, there were around 155,000 Han and Hui Chinese in northern Xinjiang and somewhat more than twice that number of Uyghurs in southern Xinjiang.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> A census of Xinjiang under Qing rule in the early 19th century tabulated ethnic shares of the population as 30% <a href="/wiki/Han_Chinese" title="Han Chinese">Han</a> and 60% <a href="/wiki/Turkic_peoples" title="Turkic peoples">Turkic</a>, while it dramatically shifted to 6% Han and 75% Uyghur in the 1953 census, however a situation similar to the Qing era-demographics with a large number of Han has been restored as of 2000 with 40.57% Han and 45.21% Uyghur.<sup id="cite_ref-ddx_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ddx-34">[34]</a></sup> Professor Stanley W. Toops noted that today's demographic situation is similar to that of the early Qing period in Xinjiang. In northern Xinjiang, the Qing brought in Han, Hui, Uyghur, Xibe, and Kazakh colonists after they <a href="/wiki/Zunghar_genocide" class="mw-redirect" title="Zunghar genocide">exterminated the Zunghar Oirat Mongols</a> in the region, with one third of Xinjiang's total population consisting of Hui and Han in the northern are, while around two thirds were Uyghurs in southern Xinjiang's Tarim Basin.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup></p>
<p>Although current PRC minority policy, which is based on <a href="/wiki/Affirmative_action_in_China" title="Affirmative action in China">affirmative actions</a>, has reinforced a Uyghur ethnic identity that is distinct from the Han population,<sup id="cite_ref-bovingdon4_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bovingdon4-36">[36]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-dillon51_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dillon51-37">[37]</a></sup> some scholars argue that Beijing unofficially favours a monolingual, monocultural model that is based on the majority.<sup id="cite_ref-Gladney_24-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gladney-24">[24]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Dwyer_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dwyer-38">[38]</a></sup> The authorities also crack down on any activity that appears to constitute separatism.<sup id="cite_ref-dillon51_37-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dillon51-37">[37]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-bovingdon19_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bovingdon19-39">[39]</a></sup> These policies, in addition to long-standing cultural differences,<sup id="cite_ref-cecChina_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cecChina-40">[40]</a></sup> have sometimes resulted in "resentments" between Uyghur and Han citizens.<sup id="cite_ref-sautman35_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sautman35-41">[41]</a></sup> On one hand, as a result of Han immigration and government policies, Uyghurs' freedoms of religion and of movement are curtailed,<sup id="cite_ref-mooreblog_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mooreblog-42">[42]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-bovingdon34_35_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bovingdon34_35-43">[43]</a></sup> while most Uyghurs argue that the government deliberately downplays their history and traditional culture.<sup id="cite_ref-Gladney_24-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gladney-24">[24]</a></sup> On the other hand, some Han citizens view Uyghurs as benefiting from special treatment, such as preferential admission to universities and exemption from the <a href="/wiki/One-child_policy" title="One-child policy">one-child policy</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-sautman29_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sautman29-44">[44]</a></sup> and as "harbouring separatist aspirations".<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup></p>
<p>Tensions between Uyghurs and Han have resulted in waves of protest in recent years.<sup id="cite_ref-Hierman_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hierman-46">[46]</a></sup> Xinjiang has been the location of several instances of violence and ethnic clashes, such as the <a href="/wiki/Ghulja_Incident" class="mw-redirect" title="Ghulja Incident">Ghulja Incident</a> of 1997, the <a href="/wiki/2008_Kashgar_attack" title="2008 Kashgar attack">2008 Kashgar attack</a>, <a href="/wiki/2008_Uyghur_unrest" title="2008 Uyghur unrest">widespread unrest</a> preceding the <a href="/wiki/2008_Summer_Olympics" title="2008 Summer Olympics">Olympic Games in Beijing</a>, as well as numerous minor attacks.<sup id="cite_ref-CACI_25-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CACI-25">[25]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Gunaratna_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gunaratna-47">[47]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Immediate_causes">Immediate causes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=July_2009_%C3%9Cr%C3%BCmqi_riots&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Immediate causes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="noviewer thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:242px">
<div style="position:relative;width:240px;border:1px solid lightgray"><a href="/wiki/File:China_edcp_location_map.svg" class="image" title="Shaoguan is located in the southeast of China, a considerable distance from Ürümqi"><img alt="Shaoguan is located in the southeast of China, a considerable distance from Ürümqi" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/China_edcp_location_map.svg/240px-China_edcp_location_map.svg.png" width="240" height="191" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/China_edcp_location_map.svg/360px-China_edcp_location_map.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/China_edcp_location_map.svg/480px-China_edcp_location_map.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1181" data-file-height="940" /></a>
<div style="position:absolute;top:81.457%;left:67.932%">
<div style="position:absolute;left:-4px;top:-4px;line-height:0"><img alt="Shaoguan" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/0/0c/Red_pog.svg/8px-Red_pog.svg.png" title="Shaoguan" width="8" height="8" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/0/0c/Red_pog.svg/12px-Red_pog.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/0/0c/Red_pog.svg/16px-Red_pog.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="64" data-file-height="64" /></div>
<div style="font-size:90%;line-height:110%;position:absolute;width:6em;top:-0.75em;right:5px;text-align:right"><span style="padding:1px;float:right;background-color:#FFFFFF">Shaoguan</span></div>
</div>
<div style="position:absolute;top:31.342%;left:25.859%">
<div style="position:absolute;left:-2px;top:-2px;line-height:0"><img alt="Ürümqi" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Green_pog.svg/4px-Green_pog.svg.png" title="Ürümqi" width="4" height="4" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Green_pog.svg/6px-Green_pog.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Green_pog.svg/8px-Green_pog.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="64" data-file-height="64" /></div>
<div style="font-size:90%;line-height:110%;position:absolute;width:6em;top:-0.75em;right:3px;text-align:right"><span style="padding:1px;float:right;background-color:#FFFFFF">Ürümqi</span></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:China_edcp_location_map.svg" title="File:China edcp location map.svg"></a></div>
Shaoguan, the location of <a href="/wiki/Shaoguan_incident" title="Shaoguan incident">the incident</a> that sparked protests in July 2009. Ürümqi is marked in green.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The riots took place several days after <a href="/wiki/Shaoguan_incident" title="Shaoguan incident">a violent incident in Shaoguan, Guangdong</a>, where many migrant workers are employed as part of a programme to alleviate labour shortages. According to state media, a disgruntled former worker disseminated rumours in late June that two Han women had been raped by six Uyghur men.<sup id="cite_ref-nyt090705_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nyt090705-9">[9]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> Official sources later said they found no evidence to support the rape allegation.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> Overnight on 25–26 June, tensions at the Guangdong factory led to a full-blown ethnic brawl between Uyghurs and Hans, during which two Uyghur co-workers were killed.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> Exiled Uyghur leaders alleged the death toll was much higher.<sup id="cite_ref-bloomberg_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bloomberg-51">[51]</a></sup> While the official <a href="/wiki/Xinhua_News_Agency" title="Xinhua News Agency">Xinhua News Agency</a> reported that the person responsible for spreading the rumours had been arrested, Uyghurs alleged that the authorities had failed to protect the Uyghur workers, or to arrest any of the Han people involved in the killings.<sup id="cite_ref-bloomberg_51-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bloomberg-51">[51]</a></sup> They organised a street protest in Ürümqi on 5 July to voice their discontent<sup id="cite_ref-nyt090705_9-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nyt090705-9">[9]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-reut090705_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-reut090705-10">[10]</a></sup> and to demand a full government investigation.<sup id="cite_ref-GladneyInterview_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GladneyInterview-52">[52]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Sauerbrey,_Kadeer_and_Seytoff_2006.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Three people seated in a small room. In the centre is a middle-aged woman with black hair in braids, a red shirt and a Uyghur doppa hat." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Sauerbrey%2C_Kadeer_and_Seytoff_2006.jpg/220px-Sauerbrey%2C_Kadeer_and_Seytoff_2006.jpg" width="220" height="111" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Sauerbrey%2C_Kadeer_and_Seytoff_2006.jpg/330px-Sauerbrey%2C_Kadeer_and_Seytoff_2006.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/1/1e/Sauerbrey%2C_Kadeer_and_Seytoff_2006.jpg 2x" data-file-width="400" data-file-height="201" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Sauerbrey,_Kadeer_and_Seytoff_2006.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The PRC government alleged that <a href="/wiki/Rebiya_Kadeer" title="Rebiya Kadeer">Rebiya Kadeer</a> (centre) played a central role in instigating the riots.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>At some point the demonstration became violent. A government statement called the riots a "pre-empted, organised violent crime [...] instigated and directed from abroad, and carried out by outlaws."<sup id="cite_ref-chinad090706_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-chinad090706-53">[53]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Nur_Bekri" title="Nur Bekri">Nur Bekri</a>, chairman of the Xinjiang regional government, said on 6 July that overseas separatist forces had taken advantage of the Shaoguan incident "to instigate Sunday's unrest and undermine the ethnic unity and social stability".<sup id="cite_ref-chinad090706_53-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-chinad090706-53">[53]</a></sup> The government blamed the exiled independence group World Uyghur Congress (WUC) for coordinating and instigating the riots over the internet.<sup id="cite_ref-chinad090706_53-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-chinad090706-53">[53]</a></sup> Government sources blamed the WUC leader Rebiya Kadeer in particular, citing her public speeches after the Tibetan unrest and phone recordings in which she had allegedly said that something would happen in Ürümqi.<sup id="cite_ref-WUCbehind_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WUCbehind-54">[54]</a></sup> Chinese authorities accused a man who they alleged to be a key WUC member of inciting ethnic tensions by circulating a violent video, and urging Uyghurs, in an online forum, to "fight back [against Hans] with violence".<sup id="cite_ref-Mukadaisi_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mukadaisi-55">[55]</a></sup> <a href="/w/index.php?title=Jirla_Isamuddin&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Jirla Isamuddin (page does not exist)">Jirla Isamuddin</a>, the mayor of Ürümqi, claimed that the protesters had organised online via such services as <a href="/wiki/Tencent_QQ" title="Tencent QQ">QQ</a> Groups.<sup id="cite_ref-cctv2_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cctv2-56">[56]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/China_Daily" title="China Daily">China Daily</a></i> asserted that the riots were organised to fuel separatism and to benefit Middle East terrorist organisations.<sup id="cite_ref-plantohelp_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-plantohelp-57">[57]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-nerve_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nerve-58">[58]</a></sup> Kadeer denied fomenting the violence,<sup id="cite_ref-profile050317_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-profile050317-12">[12]</a></sup> and argued that the Ürümqi protests and their descent into violence were triggered by heavy policing, discontent over Shaoguan and "years of Chinese repression", rather than by the intervention of separatists or terrorists;<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> Uyghur exile groups claimed that violence erupted when police used excessive force to disperse the crowd.<sup id="cite_ref-Timewestwar_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Timewestwar-13">[13]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-afp090706_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-afp090706-14">[14]</a></sup></p>
<p>All parties, then, agree that the <i>protests</i> were organised beforehand; the main points of contention are whether the <i>violence</i> was planned or spontaneous,<sup id="cite_ref-shadows_quote_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-shadows_quote-60">[60]</a></sup> and whether the underlying tensions reflect separatist inclinations or a desire for social justice.<sup id="cite_ref-GladneyInterview_52-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GladneyInterview-52">[52]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Events">Events</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=July_2009_%C3%9Cr%C3%BCmqi_riots&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Events">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Initial_demonstrations">Initial demonstrations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=July_2009_%C3%9Cr%C3%BCmqi_riots&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Initial demonstrations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Urumqiriots2009-map.svg" class="image"><img alt="Road map of Ürümqi, showing where protests occurred and where they escalated, and where police were dispatched. Protests occurred at the Grand Bazaar in the centre of the map, at People's Square in the northeast, and at the intersection of Longquan and Jiefang Roads in between; protests escalated at the latter two locations. Police were later dispatched to two locations south of the Grand Bazaar." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Urumqiriots2009-map.svg/300px-Urumqiriots2009-map.svg.png" width="300" height="270" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Urumqiriots2009-map.svg/450px-Urumqiriots2009-map.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Urumqiriots2009-map.svg/600px-Urumqiriots2009-map.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="900" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Urumqiriots2009-map.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Locations where protests and confrontations reportedly occurred</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Demonstrations began on the evening of 5 July with a protest in the <a href="/wiki/Grand_Bazaar_(%C3%9Cr%C3%BCmqi)" title="Grand Bazaar (Ürümqi)">Grand Bazaar</a>, a prominent tourist site,<sup id="cite_ref-GladneyInterview_52-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GladneyInterview-52">[52]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-guardian_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardian-61">[61]</a></sup> and crowd reportedly gathering at the <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Square_(%C3%9Cr%C3%BCmqi)" title="People's Square (Ürümqi)">People's Square</a> area.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> The demonstration began peacefully,<sup id="cite_ref-reut090705_10-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-reut090705-10">[10]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-cctv2_56-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cctv2-56">[56]</a></sup> and official and eyewitness accounts reported that it involved about 1,000 Uyghurs;<sup id="cite_ref-bbc_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc-6">[6]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-aljazeera_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aljazeera-63">[63]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Forbes_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Forbes-64">[64]</a></sup> the WUC said approximately 10,000 protesters took part.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc_6-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc-6">[6]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 6 July, XUAR chairman Nur Bekri presented an official timeline of the previous day's events, according to which more than 200 demonstrators gathered in People's Square in Ürümqi at about 5&#160;p.m. local time, and about 70 of their leaders were detained. Later, a crowd gathered in the mostly Uyghur areas of South Jiefang Road, Erdaoqiao, and Shanxi Alley; by 7:30&#160;p.m., more than one thousand were gathered in front of a hospital in Shanxi Alley. At about 7:40&#160;p.m., more than 300 people blocked the roads in the Renmin Road and Nanmen area. According to Bekri, rioters began to smash buses at 8:18&#160;p.m., after police "controlled and dispersed" the crowd.<sup id="cite_ref-.E4.B8.AD.E6.96.B0.E7.BD.91_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-.E4.B8.AD.E6.96.B0.E7.BD.91-65">[65]</a></sup></p>
<p>How the demonstrations became violent is unclear.<sup id="cite_ref-ai_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ai-66">[66]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-afraidtoevenlook_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-afraidtoevenlook-67">[67]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-buqingchu_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-buqingchu-68">[68]</a></sup> Some say the police used excessive force against the protesters;<sup id="cite_ref-ai_66-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ai-66">[66]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BBC090707_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC090707-69">[69]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-lat090706_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lat090706-70">[70]</a></sup> the World Uyghur Congress quickly issued press releases saying that the police had used deadly force and killed "scores" of protesters.<sup id="cite_ref-WUCpressrelease1_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WUCpressrelease1-71">[71]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-WUCpressrelease2_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WUCpressrelease2-72">[72]</a></sup> Kadeer has alleged that there were <i><a href="/wiki/Agent_provocateur" title="Agent provocateur">agents provocateurs</a></i> among the crowds.<sup id="cite_ref-nottelling_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nottelling-73">[73]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-csm_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-csm-74">[74]</a></sup> Others claim that the protesters initiated the violence; for example, an Uyghur eyewitness cited by <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i> said protesters began throwing rocks at the police.<sup id="cite_ref-nyt090705_9-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nyt090705-9">[9]</a></sup> The government's official line was that the violence was not only initiated by the protesters, but also had been premeditated and coordinated by Uyghur separatists abroad.<sup id="cite_ref-chinad090706_53-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-chinad090706-53">[53]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-cctv2_56-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cctv2-56">[56]</a></sup> The local <a href="/wiki/Chinese_public_security_bureau" title="Chinese public security bureau">public security bureau</a> said it found evidence that many Uyghurs had travelled from other cities to gather for the riot, and that they had begun preparing weapons two or three days before the riot.<sup id="cite_ref-xhweapons_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-xhweapons-75">[75]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Escalation_and_spread">Escalation and spread</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=July_2009_%C3%9Cr%C3%BCmqi_riots&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Escalation and spread">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>After the confrontation with police turned violent, rioters began hurling rocks, smashing vehicles, breaking into shops, and attacking Han civilians.<sup id="cite_ref-nyt090705_9-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nyt090705-9">[9]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Timewestwar_13-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Timewestwar-13">[13]</a></sup> At least 1,000 Uyghurs were involved in the rioting when it began,<sup id="cite_ref-bbc_6-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc-6">[6]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-aljazeera_63-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aljazeera-63">[63]</a></sup> and the number of rioters may have risen to as many as 3,000.<sup id="cite_ref-timesonline_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-timesonline-11">[11]</a></sup> Jane Macartney of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Times" title="The Times">The Times</a></i> characterised the first day's rioting as consisting mainly of "Han stabbed by marauding gangs of Uighurs";<sup id="cite_ref-times-escalates_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-times-escalates-76">[76]</a></sup> a report in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Australian" title="The Australian">The Australian</a></i> several months later suggested that religiously moderate Uyghurs may also have been attacked by rioters.<sup id="cite_ref-shadows_19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-shadows-19">[19]</a></sup> Although the majority of rioters were Uyghur, not all Uyghurs were violent during the riots; there are accounts of Han and Uyghur civilians helping each other escape the violence and hide.<sup id="cite_ref-kindness_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kindness-77">[77]</a></sup> About 1,000 police officers were dispatched; they used batons, live ammunition, <a href="/wiki/Electroshock_weapon" title="Electroshock weapon">tasers</a>, tear gas and water hoses to disperse the rioters, and set up roadblocks and posted armoured vehicles throughout the city.<sup id="cite_ref-afp090706_14-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-afp090706-14">[14]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-guardian_61-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardian-61">[61]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-aljazeera_63-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aljazeera-63">[63]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ai_66-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ai-66">[66]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:290px;">
<div id="mwe_player_0" class="PopUpMediaTransform" style="width:288px;" videopayload="&lt;div class=&quot;mediaContainer&quot; style=&quot;width:352px&quot;&gt;&lt;video id=&quot;mwe_player_1&quot; poster=&quot;//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/%C3%9Cr%C3%BCmqi_riots_video.ogv/352px--%C3%9Cr%C3%BCmqi_riots_video.ogv.jpg&quot; controls=&quot;&quot; preload=&quot;none&quot; autoplay=&quot;&quot; style=&quot;width:352px;height:288px&quot; class=&quot;kskin&quot; data-durationhint=&quot;66.496&quot; data-startoffset=&quot;0&quot; data-mwtitle=&quot;Ürümqi_riots_video.ogv&quot; data-mwprovider=&quot;wikimediacommons&quot;&gt;&lt;source src=&quot;//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/1/17/%C3%9Cr%C3%BCmqi_riots_video.ogv&quot; type=&quot;video/ogg; codecs=&amp;quot;theora, vorbis&amp;quot;&quot; data-title=&quot;Original Ogg file, 352 × 288 (632 kbps)&quot; data-shorttitle=&quot;Ogg source&quot; data-width=&quot;352&quot; data-height=&quot;288&quot; data-bandwidth=&quot;632341&quot; data-framerate=&quot;15&quot;/&gt;&lt;source src=&quot;//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/1/17/%C3%9Cr%C3%BCmqi_riots_video.ogv/%C3%9Cr%C3%BCmqi_riots_video.ogv.160p.ogv&quot; type=&quot;video/ogg; codecs=&amp;quot;theora, vorbis&amp;quot;&quot; data-title=&quot;Low bandwidth Ogg video (160P)&quot; data-shorttitle=&quot;Ogg 160P&quot; data-transcodekey=&quot;160p.ogv&quot; data-width=&quot;196&quot; data-height=&quot;160&quot; data-bandwidth=&quot;176088&quot; data-framerate=&quot;15&quot;/&gt;&lt;/video&gt;&lt;/div&gt;"><img alt="File:Ürümqi riots video.ogv" style="width:288px;height:236px" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/%C3%9Cr%C3%BCmqi_riots_video.ogv/288px-seek%3D49-%C3%9Cr%C3%BCmqi_riots_video.ogv.jpg" /><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/1/17/%C3%9Cr%C3%BCmqi_riots_video.ogv" title="Play media" target="new"><span class="play-btn-large"><span class="mw-tmh-playtext">Play media</span></span></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:%C3%9Cr%C3%BCmqi_riots_video.ogv" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Footage of the first day's violence, captured on a witness' cell phone</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>During a press conference, Mayor Jirla Isamuddin said that at about 8:15&#160;p.m., some protesters started to fight and loot, overturned guardrails and smashed three buses before being dispersed.<sup id="cite_ref-cctv2_56-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cctv2-56">[56]</a></sup> At 8:30&#160;p.m., violence escalated around South Jiefang Road and Longquan Street area, with rioters torching police patrol cars and attacking passers-by.<sup id="cite_ref-cctv2_56-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cctv2-56">[56]</a></sup> Soon, between 700 and 800 people went from the People's Square to Daximen and Xiaoximen area, "fighting, smashing, looting, torching and killing" along the way. At 9:30&#160;p.m., the government received reports that three people had been killed and 26 injured, 6 of whom were police officers.<sup id="cite_ref-cctv2_56-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cctv2-56">[56]</a></sup> Police reinforcements were dispatched to hotspots of Renmin Road, Nanmen, Tuanjie Road, Yan'An Road and South Xinhua Road. Police took control of the main roadways and commercial districts in the city at around 10&#160;pm, but riots continued in side streets and alleyways, with Hans attacked and cars overturned or torched, according to the mayor.<sup id="cite_ref-cctv2_56-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cctv2-56">[56]</a></sup> Police then formed small teams and "swept" the entire city for the next two days.<sup id="cite_ref-cctv2_56-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cctv2-56">[56]</a></sup> A strict curfew was put in place;<sup id="cite_ref-HuG8_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HuG8-78">[78]</a></sup> authorities imposed "comprehensive traffic control" from 9:00&#160;pm Tuesday to 8:00&#160;am Wednesday "to avoid further chaos".<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup></p>
<p>The official news agency, Xinhua, reported that police believed agitators were trying to organise more unrest in other areas in Xinjiang, such as <a href="/wiki/Aksu,_Xinjiang" title="Aksu, Xinjiang">Aksu</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Ili_Kazakh_Autonomous_Prefecture" title="Ili Kazakh Autonomous Prefecture">Yili Prefecture</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC090707_69-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC090707-69">[69]</a></sup> Violent protests also sprang up in <a href="/wiki/Kashgar" title="Kashgar">Kashgar</a>, in southwestern Xinjiang,<sup id="cite_ref-npr_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-npr-80">[80]</a></sup> where the <i>South China Morning Post</i> reported many shops were closed, and the area around the mosque was sealed off by a <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Liberation_Army" title="People's Liberation Army">People's Liberation Army</a> platoon after confrontations. Local Uyghurs blamed the security forces for using excessive force—they "attacked the protesters and arrested 50 people".<sup id="cite_ref-SCMPeerie_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SCMPeerie-81">[81]</a></sup> Another clash was reported near the mosque on Tuesday, 7 July, and an estimated 50 people were arrested. Up to 12,000 students at the Kashgar Teaching Institute were confined to campus since Sunday's riots, according to the <i>Post</i>. Many of the institute's students had apparently travelled to Ürümqi for the demonstrations there.<sup id="cite_ref-SCMPcollege_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SCMPcollege-82">[82]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Casualties_and_damage">Casualties and damage</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=July_2009_%C3%9Cr%C3%BCmqi_riots&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Casualties and damage">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>During the first hours of the rioting, state media only reported that three people had been killed.<sup id="cite_ref-reut090705_10-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-reut090705-10">[10]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-afp090706_14-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-afp090706-14">[14]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> The number rose sharply, though, after the first night's rioting; at midday on Monday, 6 July, Xinhua announced that 129 people had died.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> In the following days the death toll reported by various government sources (including Xinhua and party officials) gradually grew, with the last official update on 18 July placing the tally at 197 dead,<sup id="cite_ref-CD197_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CD197-1">[1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Xinhua197_2-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Xinhua197-2">[2]</a></sup> 1,721 injured.<sup id="cite_ref-scmp20090717_3-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-scmp20090717-3">[3]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-NYTtrials_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYTtrials-4">[4]</a></sup> The World Uyghur Congress has claimed that the death toll was around 600.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc_6-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc-6">[6]</a></sup></p>
<p>Xinhua did not immediately disclose the ethnic breakdown of the dead,<sup id="cite_ref-npr_80-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-npr-80">[80]</a></sup> but journalists from <i>The Times</i> and <i>The Daily Telegraph</i> reported that most of the victims appeared to have been Han.<sup id="cite_ref-mooreblog_42-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mooreblog-42">[42]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> For instance, on 10 July Xinhua stated that 137 of the dead (out of the total of 184 that was being reported at that time) were Han, 46 Uyghur, and 1 <a href="/wiki/Hui_people" title="Hui people">Hui</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-XH184dead_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-XH184dead-86">[86]</a></sup> There were casualties among the rioters as well;<sup id="cite_ref-ai_66-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ai-66">[66]</a></sup> for example, according to official accounts, a group of 12 rioters attacking civilians were shot by police.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup> In the months following the riots, the government maintained that the majority of casualties were Han<sup id="cite_ref-BBC1500_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC1500-16">[16]</a></sup> and hospitals said that two-thirds of the injured were Han,<sup id="cite_ref-Timewestwar_13-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Timewestwar-13">[13]</a></sup> although the World Uyghur Congress claims that many Uyghurs were killed as well.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC1500_16-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC1500-16">[16]</a></sup> According to the official count released by the Chinese government in August 2009, 134 of the 156 civilian victims were Han, 11 Hui, 10 Uyghur, and 1 <a href="/wiki/Manchu" class="mw-redirect" title="Manchu">Manchu</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-XHaugustbreakdown_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-XHaugustbreakdown-89">[89]</a></sup> Uyghur advocates continue to question these figures, saying that the number of ethnic Uyghurs remains understated.<sup id="cite_ref-afraidtoevenlook_67-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-afraidtoevenlook-67">[67]</a></sup> Xinhua reported that 627 vehicles and 633 constructions were damaged.<sup id="cite_ref-xhinjured_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-xhinjured-90">[90]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Ürümqi municipal government initially announced that it would pay <a href="/wiki/Chinese_yuan" title="Chinese yuan">¥</a>200,000 as compensation, plus another ¥10,000 as "funeral expense" for every "innocent death" caused by the riot.<sup id="cite_ref-caijing_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-caijing-91">[91]</a></sup> The compensation was later doubled to ¥420,000 per death.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup> Mayor Jirla Isamuddin estimated that the compensations will cost at least ¥100&#160;million.<sup id="cite_ref-caijing_91-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-caijing-91">[91]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="After_5_July">After 5 July</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=July_2009_%C3%9Cr%C3%BCmqi_riots&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: After 5 July">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The city remained tense while journalists invited into the city witnessed confrontational scenes between Chinese troops and Uyghurs demanding the release of family members who they said had been "arbitrarily" arrested.<sup id="cite_ref-times-escalates_76-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-times-escalates-76">[76]</a></sup> Uyghur women told <i>The Daily Telegraph</i> reporter that police entered Uyghur districts in the night of 6 July, burst through doors, pulled men and boys from their beds, and rounded up 100 suspects.<sup id="cite_ref-dt5769839_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dt5769839-93">[93]</a></sup> By 7 July, officials reported that 1,434 suspected rioters had been arrested.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup> A group of 200 to 300 Uyghur women assembled on 7 July to protest what they said was "indiscriminate" detention of Uyghur men; the protest led to a tense but non-violent confrontation with police forces.<sup id="cite_ref-womensprotest_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-womensprotest-95">[95]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Fosterpolice_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fosterpolice-96">[96]</a></sup> Rebiya Kadeer claimed that "nearly 10,000 people" had gone missing overnight.<sup id="cite_ref-Reut20090729_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Reut20090729-97">[97]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Human_Rights_Watch" title="Human Rights Watch">Human Rights Watch</a> (HRW) later documented 43 cases of Uyghur men who disappeared after being taken away by Chinese security forces in large-scale sweeps of Uyghur neighbourhoods overnight on 6–7 July,<sup id="cite_ref-afraidtoevenlook_67-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-afraidtoevenlook-67">[67]</a></sup> and said that this was likely to be "just the tip of the iceberg";<sup id="cite_ref-BBC8317644_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC8317644-8">[8]</a></sup> HRW allege that young men, mostly in their 20s, had been unlawfully arrested and have not been seen or heard from as of 20 October 2009<sup id="cite_ref-afraidtoevenlook_67-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-afraidtoevenlook-67">[67]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 7 July, there were large-scale armed demonstrations<sup id="cite_ref-bno_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bno-98">[98]</a></sup> by ethnic Han in Ürümqi.<sup id="cite_ref-telegraphmob_99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-telegraphmob-99">[99]</a></sup> Conflicting estimates of the Han demonstrators' numbers were reported by the western media and varied from "hundreds"<sup id="cite_ref-bno_98-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bno-98">[98]</a></sup> to as high as 10,000.<sup id="cite_ref-telegraphmob_99-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-telegraphmob-99">[99]</a></sup> <i>The Times</i> reported that smaller fights were frequently breaking out between Uyghurs and Hans, and that groups of Han citizens had organised to take revenge on "Uyghur mobs".<sup id="cite_ref-times-escalates_76-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-times-escalates-76">[76]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-telegraphmob_99-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-telegraphmob-99">[99]</a></sup> Police used tear gas and roadblocks in an attempt to disperse the demonstration,<sup id="cite_ref-rte_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rte-100">[100]</a></sup> and urged Han citizens over loudspeakers to "calm down" and "let the police do their job".<sup id="cite_ref-telegraphmob_99-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-telegraphmob-99">[99]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Li_Zhi_(official)" class="mw-redirect" title="Li Zhi (official)">Li Zhi</a>, <a href="/wiki/CPC_party_chief" class="mw-redirect" title="CPC party chief">party chief</a> of Ürümqi, stood on the roof of a police car with a megaphone appealing to the crowd to go home.<sup id="cite_ref-dt5769839_93-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dt5769839-93">[93]</a></sup></p>
<p>Mass protests had been quelled by 8 July, although sporadic violence was reported.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-SCMPconflict_103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SCMPconflict-103">[103]</a></sup> In the days after the riots, "thousands" of people tried to leave the city, and the price for bus tickets rose as much as fivefold.<sup id="cite_ref-bbcJ10_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbcJ10-17">[17]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 10 July, city authorities closed Ürümqi mosques "for public safety", saying it was too dangerous to have large gatherings and that holding <i><a href="/wiki/Jumu%27ah" title="Jumu'ah">Jumu'ah</a></i>, traditional Friday prayers, could reignite tensions.<sup id="cite_ref-bbcJ10_17-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbcJ10-17">[17]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-euronewsJume_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-euronewsJume-105">[105]</a></sup> Large crowds of Uyghurs gathered for prayer anyway, however, and police decided to let two mosques open to avoid having an "incident".<sup id="cite_ref-bbcJ10_17-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbcJ10-17">[17]</a></sup> After prayers at the White Mosque, several hundred people demonstrated over people detained after the riot,<sup id="cite_ref-rtrj10_106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rtrj10-106">[106]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup> but were dispersed by riot police, with five or six people arrested.<sup id="cite_ref-rtrj10_106-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rtrj10-106">[106]</a></sup></p>
<p>Over 300 more people were reported arrested in early August. According to the BBC, the total number of arrests in connection with the riots was over 1,500.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC1500_16-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC1500-16">[16]</a></sup> <i>The Financial Times</i> estimated that the number was higher, citing an insider saying that some 4,000 arrests had already taken place by mid July, and that Ürümqi's prisons were so full that newly arrested people were being held in a People's Liberation Army warehouse.<sup id="cite_ref-FT5aa932ee_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FT5aa932ee-108">[108]</a></sup> According to the Uyghur American Association, several other Uyghur journalists and bloggers were also detained after the riots; one of them, journalist Gheyret Niyaz, was later sentenced to 15 years in prison for having spoken to foreign media.<sup id="cite_ref-Niyaz_109-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Niyaz-109">[109]</a></sup> In the most high-profile case, <a href="/wiki/Ilham_Tohti" title="Ilham Tohti">Ilham Tohti</a>, an ethnic Uyghur economist at <a href="/wiki/Minzu_University_of_China" title="Minzu University of China">Minzu University of China</a>, was arrested two days after the riots over his criticisms of the Xinjiang government.<sup id="cite_ref-rfajul082009_110-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rfajul082009-110">[110]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-rfa0824en_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rfa0824en-111">[111]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-release_112-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-release-112">[112]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Reactions_and_response">Reactions and response</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=July_2009_%C3%9Cr%C3%BCmqi_riots&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Reactions and response">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Domestic_reaction">Domestic reaction</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=July_2009_%C3%9Cr%C3%BCmqi_riots&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Domestic reaction">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Communications_black-out">Communications black-out</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=July_2009_%C3%9Cr%C3%BCmqi_riots&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Communications black-out">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Mobile phone service and internet access were limited both during and after the riots. China Mobile phone service was cut "to prevent the incident from spreading further".<sup id="cite_ref-ChinaMobilecut_113-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ChinaMobilecut-113">[113]</a></sup> Outbound international calls throughout Xinjiang were blocked,<sup id="cite_ref-SCMPoverseas_114-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SCMPoverseas-114">[114]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-DemocracyNowvideo_115-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DemocracyNowvideo-115">[115]</a></sup> and Internet connections in the region had been locked down<sup id="cite_ref-reuters1_116-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-reuters1-116">[116]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-comm_cut_117-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-comm_cut-117">[117]</a></sup> or non-local websites blocked. Reporting from Ürümqi's Hoi Tak Hotel on 9 July, <i><a href="/wiki/Aljazeera" class="mw-redirect" title="Aljazeera">Aljazeera</a></i> reported that the foreign journalists' hotel was the only place in the city with Internet access, although the journalist could not send text messages or place international phone calls.<sup id="cite_ref-DemocracyNowvideo_115-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DemocracyNowvideo-115">[115]</a></sup> Many unauthorised postings on local sites and Google were removed by censors;<sup id="cite_ref-afraidtoevenlook_67-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-afraidtoevenlook-67">[67]</a></sup> images and video footage of the demonstrations and rioting, however, were soon found posted on Twitter, YouTube, and <a href="/wiki/Flickr" title="Flickr">Flickr</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup> Many Xinjiang-based websites became inaccessible worldwide,<sup id="cite_ref-bloomberg_51-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bloomberg-51">[51]</a></sup> and internet access within Ürümqi remained restricted nearly a year following the riots;<sup id="cite_ref-MissingLink_119-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MissingLink-119">[119]</a></sup> it was not restored until 14 May 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-InternetRestored_120-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-InternetRestored-120">[120]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Government">Government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=July_2009_%C3%9Cr%C3%BCmqi_riots&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Chinese state-controlled television broadcast graphic footage of cars being smashed and people being beaten.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup> Officials reiterated the party line: XUAR chairman Nur Bekri delivered a lengthy address on the situation and on the <a href="/wiki/Shaoguan_incident" title="Shaoguan incident">Shaoguan incident</a>, and claimed that the government of both Guangdong and Xinjiang had dealt with the deaths of the workers properly and with respect. Bekri further condemned the riots as "premeditated and planned";<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup> Eligen Imibakhi, chairman of the Standing Committee of the Xinjiang Regional People's Congress, blamed 5 July riots on "extremism, separatism and terrorism".<sup id="cite_ref-netease1_123-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-netease1-123">[123]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-abcnews1_124-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-abcnews1-124">[124]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Hu_Jintao_during_a_defense_meeting_held_at_the_Pentagon,_May_2002,_cropped.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Bespectacled Asian man in suit" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Hu_Jintao_during_a_defense_meeting_held_at_the_Pentagon%2C_May_2002%2C_cropped.jpg/170px-Hu_Jintao_during_a_defense_meeting_held_at_the_Pentagon%2C_May_2002%2C_cropped.jpg" width="170" height="211" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Hu_Jintao_during_a_defense_meeting_held_at_the_Pentagon%2C_May_2002%2C_cropped.jpg/255px-Hu_Jintao_during_a_defense_meeting_held_at_the_Pentagon%2C_May_2002%2C_cropped.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Hu_Jintao_during_a_defense_meeting_held_at_the_Pentagon%2C_May_2002%2C_cropped.jpg/340px-Hu_Jintao_during_a_defense_meeting_held_at_the_Pentagon%2C_May_2002%2C_cropped.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1484" data-file-height="1844" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Hu_Jintao_during_a_defense_meeting_held_at_the_Pentagon,_May_2002,_cropped.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The riots prompted PRC president <a href="/wiki/Hu_Jintao" title="Hu Jintao">Hu Jintao</a> to return from the international <a href="/wiki/35th_G8_summit" title="35th G8 summit">G8 summit</a> early.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Chinese media covered the rioting extensively.<sup id="cite_ref-ft00144_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ft00144-15">[15]</a></sup> Hours after troops stopped the rioting, the state invited foreign journalists on an official fact-finding trip to Ürümqi;<sup id="cite_ref-nyt090708_125-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nyt090708-125">[125]</a></sup> journalists from more than 100 media organisations were all corralled into the downtown Hoi Tak Hotel,<sup id="cite_ref-SCMPoverseas_114-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SCMPoverseas-114">[114]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-DemocracyNowvideo_115-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DemocracyNowvideo-115">[115]</a></sup> sharing 30 internet connections.<sup id="cite_ref-SCMPoverseas_114-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SCMPoverseas-114">[114]</a></sup> Journalists were given unprecedented access to troublespots and hospitals.<sup id="cite_ref-pfteleg090707_126-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pfteleg090707-126">[126]</a></sup> The <i>Financial Times</i> referred to this handling as an improvement, compared to the "public-relations disaster" of the Tibetan unrest in 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-ft00144_15-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ft00144-15">[15]</a></sup></p>
<p>In an effort to soothe tensions immediately after the riots, state media began a mass publicity campaign throughout Xinjiang extolling ethnic harmony. Local television programmes united Uyghur and Han singers in a chorus of "We are all part of the same family"; Uygurs who "acted heroically" during the riots were profiled; loud-hailer trucks blasted slogans in the streets. A common slogan warned against the "<a href="/wiki/Three_Evils" title="Three Evils">three forces</a>" of terrorism, separatism and extremism.<sup id="cite_ref-SCMPpropaganda_127-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SCMPpropaganda-127">[127]</a></sup></p>
<p>President Hu Jintao curtailed his attendance of the <a href="/wiki/35th_G8_summit" title="35th G8 summit">G8 summit in Italy</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-HuG8_78-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HuG8-78">[78]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup> convened an emergency meeting of the <a href="/wiki/Politburo_of_the_Communist_Party_of_China" title="Politburo of the Communist Party of China">Politburo</a>, and dispatched Standing Committee member <a href="/wiki/Zhou_Yongkang" title="Zhou Yongkang">Zhou Yongkang</a> to Xinjiang to "guid[e] stability-preservation work in Xinjiang".<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup> <i>South China Morning Post</i> reported a government source saying Beijing would re-evaluate the impact on arrangements for the country's forthcoming 60th anniversary celebrations in October.<sup id="cite_ref-SCMPcaughtout_130-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SCMPcaughtout-130">[130]</a></sup> Guangdong's <a href="/wiki/Communist_Party_of_China" title="Communist Party of China">CPC</a> Provincial Committee Secretary, <a href="/wiki/Wang_Yang_(official)" class="mw-redirect" title="Wang Yang (official)">Wang Yang</a>, noted that the government policies towards ethnic minorities "definitely need adjustments", otherwise "there will be some problems."<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup> A security planner said the authorities planned to fly in more troops from other stations to raise the number of armed police presence to 130,000 before the 60th anniversary celebrations in October.<sup id="cite_ref-FT5aa932ee_108-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FT5aa932ee-108">[108]</a></sup></p>
<p>After the riots, the Chinese government exercised diplomatic pressure on nations that Rebiya Kadeer was scheduled to visit. In late July, India declined Kadeer a visa "on the advice of Beijing",<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup> and Beijing summoned the Japanese ambassador in protest of a trip Kadeer made to Japan.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Teleg5943780_134-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Teleg5943780-134">[134]</a></sup> When Kadeer visited Australia in August to promote a film about her life, China officially complained to the Australian government and asked for the film to be withdrawn.<sup id="cite_ref-Teleg5943780_134-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Teleg5943780-134">[134]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Internet_response">Internet response</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=July_2009_%C3%9Cr%C3%BCmqi_riots&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Internet response">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The response to the riots on the Chinese blogosphere was markedly more varied than the official response. Despite blocks and censorship, <a href="/wiki/Internet_censorship_in_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China" class="mw-redirect" title="Internet censorship in the People's Republic of China">Internet watchers</a> monitored continued attempts by netizens to publish their own thoughts on the causes of the incident or vent their anger about the violence. While some bloggers were supportive of the government, others were more reflective of the event's cause.<sup id="cite_ref-onlineventire_135-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-onlineventire-135">[135]</a></sup> On numerous forums and news sites, government workers quickly removed comments about the riots.<sup id="cite_ref-onlineventire_135-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-onlineventire-135">[135]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup> Common themes were calls for punishment for those responsible; some posts evoked the name of <a href="/wiki/Wang_Zhen_(general)" title="Wang Zhen (general)">Wang Zhen</a>, the general who is respected by Hans and other minorities, and feared by many Uyghurs for repression after the communist takeover of Xinjiang in 1949.<sup id="cite_ref-onlineventire_135-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-onlineventire-135">[135]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="International_reactions">International reactions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=July_2009_%C3%9Cr%C3%BCmqi_riots&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: International reactions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="International_organisations">International organisations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=July_2009_%C3%9Cr%C3%BCmqi_riots&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: International organisations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<ul>
<li><b>United Nations</b>: Secretary-General <a href="/wiki/Ban_Ki-moon" title="Ban Ki-moon">Ban Ki-moon</a> urged all sides to exercise restraint,<sup id="cite_ref-jg_137-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jg-137">[137]</a></sup> and called on China to take measures to protect the civilian population as well as respect the freedoms of citizens, including freedom of speech, assembly and information.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup> Human rights chief <a href="/wiki/Navi_Pillay" title="Navi Pillay">Navi Pillay</a> said she was "alarmed" over the high death toll, noting this was an "extraordinarily high number of people to be killed and injured in less than a day of rioting."<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup> She also said China must treat detainees humanely in a way that adheres to international norms.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">[141]</a></sup></li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Shanghai_Cooperation_Organisation" title="Shanghai Cooperation Organisation">Shanghai Cooperation Organisation</a></b>: said it sympathised with the family members of those innocent people killed in the riot; it said that its member states regard Xinjiang as an inalienable part of the People's Republic of China and believe the situation in Xinjiang is purely China's internal affairs.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup> Russian Foreign Minister <a href="/wiki/Sergey_Lavrov" title="Sergey Lavrov">Sergey Lavrov</a> condemned rioters for "Using separatist slogans and provoking ethnic intolerance.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup> Officials from both neighbouring <a href="/wiki/Kazakhstan" title="Kazakhstan">Kazakhstan</a><sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">[144]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Kyrgyzstan" title="Kyrgyzstan">Kyrgyzstan</a> said they were braced for "an influx of refugees" and tightened border controls.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">[145]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">[146]</a></sup> Despite the Kazakh government support, over 5,000 Uyghurs protested on 19 July in former capital <a href="/wiki/Almaty" title="Almaty">Almaty</a> against Chinese police use of deadly force against the rioters.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">[147]</a></sup></li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Organisation_of_the_Islamic_Conference" class="mw-redirect" title="Organisation of the Islamic Conference">Organisation of the Islamic Conference</a></b>: decried the "disproportionate use of force", calling on Beijing to "bring those responsible to justice swiftly" and urging China to find a solution to the unrest by examining why it had erupted.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">[148]</a></sup></li>
<li><b>European Union</b>: leaders expressed concern, and urged the Chinese government to show restraint in dealing with the protests:<sup id="cite_ref-ra_149-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ra-149">[149]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">[150]</a></sup> German Chancellor <a href="/wiki/Angela_Merkel" title="Angela Merkel">Angela Merkel</a> urged respect for the rights of minorities;<sup id="cite_ref-et_151-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-et-151">[151]</a></sup> Italian President <a href="/wiki/Giorgio_Napolitano" title="Giorgio Napolitano">Giorgio Napolitano</a> brought up human rights at a press conference with Hu Jintao, and said that "economic and social progress that is being achieved in China places new demands in terms of human rights."<sup id="cite_ref-rfe_152-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rfe-152">[152]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">[153]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Countries">Countries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=July_2009_%C3%9Cr%C3%BCmqi_riots&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Countries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Turkey, which has a vocal Uyghur minority and is a majority-Turkic nation, officially expressed "deep sadness", and urged the Chinese authorities to bring the perpetrators to justice.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">[154]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">[155]</a></sup> Its Prime Minister, <a href="/wiki/Recep_Tayyip_Erdo%C4%9Fan" title="Recep Tayyip Erdoğan">Recep Tayyip Erdoğan</a>, said the incident was "like genocide",<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">[156]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">[157]</a></sup> while Trade and Industry Minister <a href="/wiki/Nihat_Erg%C3%BCn" title="Nihat Ergün">Nihat Ergün</a> called for a boycott on Chinese goods.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">[158]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">[159]</a></sup> The violence against Uyghurs also caused lots of <a href="/wiki/Turkish_people" title="Turkish people">Turkish people</a> to gather for protests against PRC, mostly targeting Chinese embassies and consulates in Turkey's various cities. The Turkish stance sparked a significant outcry from Chinese media.<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">[160]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">[161]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">[162]</a></sup> Rebiya Kadeer claimed that Turkey is hampered from interfering with Uyghurs because it recognizes that its own <a href="/wiki/Turkey%E2%80%93PKK_conflict" class="mw-redirect" title="Turkey–PKK conflict">Kurdish issue</a> may get interfered with by China in retaliation.<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">[163]</a></sup> An appeal for Chinese products to be boycotted by <a href="/wiki/Nihat_Ergun" class="mw-redirect" title="Nihat Ergun">Nihat Ergun</a> failed.<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">[164]</a></sup></p>
<p>Arab countries politically supported China in the OIC with especially Saudi Arabia and Egypt helping China squash any potential anti-Chinese motion by the <a href="/wiki/Organisation_of_Islamic_Cooperation" title="Organisation of Islamic Cooperation">Organisation of Islamic Cooperation</a> on the Uyghurs, Egypt viewed its own internal sectarian problems like China's and Sudan was also concerned about external interference in its internal problems as well, while Indonesia had to deal with its own internal Islamists and emphasized that there was no religious conflict but instead ethnic based disturbances in Xinjiang to calm the situation down.<sup id="cite_ref-wikileaks_165-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wikileaks-165">[165]</a></sup> Pakistan, Saudi Arabia, and Egypt helped China kill off a statement on the Xinjiang situation in the OIC.<sup id="cite_ref-wikileaks2_166-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wikileaks2-166">[166]</a></sup> There has been no public reaction by the Arab League, Saudi Arabia and Iran on the situation and China has built stronger relations with Iran and Saudi Arabia due to their influence in the Islamic world.<sup id="cite_ref-Al-Tamimi2013_167-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Al-Tamimi2013-167">[167]</a></sup></p>
<p>Afghanistan,<sup id="cite_ref-afghan_168-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-afghan-168">[168]</a></sup> Cambodia,<sup id="cite_ref-cambod_169-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cambod-169">[169]</a></sup> and Vietnam said they believed the Chinese government was "taking appropriate measures",<sup id="cite_ref-viet_170-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-viet-170">[170]</a></sup> their statements backed "the territorial integrity and sovereignty of China".<sup id="cite_ref-afghan_168-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-afghan-168">[168]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Vice_President_of_the_Federated_States_of_Micronesia" title="Vice President of the Federated States of Micronesia">Micronesian Vice President</a> <a href="/wiki/Alik_Alik" class="mw-redirect" title="Alik Alik">Alik Alik</a> condemned the riot as a "terrorist act".<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">[171]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Uyghurprotest_DC_2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Demonstrators dressed in light blue, holding blue flags with white crescent. One in the foreground is wearing blue face paint." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Uyghurprotest_DC_2.jpg/220px-Uyghurprotest_DC_2.jpg" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Uyghurprotest_DC_2.jpg/330px-Uyghurprotest_DC_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Uyghurprotest_DC_2.jpg/440px-Uyghurprotest_DC_2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3712" data-file-height="2088" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Uyghurprotest_DC_2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Uyghur demonstration in Washington, D.C.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Iran said it shared the concerns of Turkey and the OIC, and appealed to the Chinese government to respect the rights of the Muslim population in Xinjiang.<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">[172]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">[173]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Japanese government was monitoring the situation, with concern;<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">[174]</a></sup> Singapore urged restraint and dialogue;<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">[175]</a></sup> while the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_China" class="mw-redirect" title="Republic of China">ROC</a> government in Taiwan strongly condemned all those who instigated the violence. Premier Liu Chiao-shiuan also urged restraint and expressed hope that the Chinese authorities will demonstrate the "greatest possible leniency and tolerance in dealing with the aftermath" and respect the rights of ethnic minorities.<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">[176]</a></sup> Taiwan denied a visa to Kadeer in September&#160;2009, alleging she had links to the <a href="/wiki/East_Turkestan_Islamic_Movement" class="mw-redirect" title="East Turkestan Islamic Movement">East Turkestan Islamic Movement</a>, classed as a terrorist organisation by the United Nations and United States.<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">[177]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Uyghur_protest_Berlin,_July_2009_3.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Street demonstration with banners, passing an official building" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Uyghur_protest_Berlin%2C_July_2009_3.jpg/220px-Uyghur_protest_Berlin%2C_July_2009_3.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Uyghur_protest_Berlin%2C_July_2009_3.jpg/330px-Uyghur_protest_Berlin%2C_July_2009_3.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Uyghur_protest_Berlin%2C_July_2009_3.jpg/440px-Uyghur_protest_Berlin%2C_July_2009_3.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Uyghur_protest_Berlin,_July_2009_3.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Demonstration in Berlin for Uyghur human rights.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Switzerland called for restraint, and sent condolences to the families of victims and urged China to respect freedom of expression and the press.<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">[178]</a></sup> Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Kevin_Rudd" title="Kevin Rudd">Kevin Rudd</a> of Australia urged restraint to bring about a "peaceful settlement to this difficulty."<sup id="cite_ref-et_151-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-et-151">[151]</a></sup> Serbia stated that it opposed separatism and supports the "resolution of all disputes by peaceful means."<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">[179]</a></sup> Belarus noted with regret the loss of life and damage in the region, and hoped that the situation would soon normalise.<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">[180]</a></sup></p>
