<p>There was violence in the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Netherlands</a> and in Norway: the Chinese embassy in the Netherlands was attacked by Uyghur activists who smashed windows with bricks,<sup id="cite_ref-rte_100-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rte-100">[100]</a></sup> the Chinese flag was also burnt.<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">[181]</a></sup> There were 142 arrests,<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">[182]</a></sup> and China closed the embassy for the day.<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">[183]</a></sup> About 100 Uyghurs protested outside the Chinese embassy in the Norwegian capital. Eleven were detained, and later released without charge.<sup id="cite_ref-ap_184-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ap-184">[184]</a></sup> Protesters from a coalition of <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Indonesia" title="Islam in Indonesia">Indonesian Islamist</a> groups attacked guards at the Chinese embassy in <a href="/wiki/Jakarta" title="Jakarta">Jakarta</a> and called for a <a href="/wiki/Jihad" title="Jihad">jihad</a> against China.<sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">[185]</a></sup> Pakistan said there were some "elements" out to harm Sino-Pakistan ties would not damage or destabilise the interests of the two countries.<sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">[186]</a></sup> Sri Lanka stressed the incident was an internal affair of China and was confident that efforts by the Chinese authorities would restore normalcy.<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">[187]</a></sup></p>
<p>Canadian Foreign Affairs Minister <a href="/wiki/Lawrence_Cannon" title="Lawrence Cannon">Lawrence Cannon</a> urged "dialogue and goodwill" to help resolve grievances and prevent further deterioration of the situation.<sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">[188]</a></sup> The spokesman for the Obama administration said the United States regretted the loss of life in Xinjiang,<sup id="cite_ref-ra_149-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ra-149">[149]</a></sup> was deeply concerned and called on all sides to exercise restraint.<sup id="cite_ref-jg_137-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jg-137">[137]</a></sup> U.S. State Department spokesman Ian Kelly, said "it's important that the Chinese authorities act to restore order and prevent further violence."<sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">[189]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/United_States_Commission_on_International_Religious_Freedom" title="United States Commission on International Religious Freedom">United States Commission on International Religious Freedom</a> expressed "grave concern" over repression in China, and called for an independent investigation on the riots and targeted sanctions against China.<sup id="cite_ref-SCMPsanct_190-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SCMPsanct-190">[190]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_organisations">Other organisations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=July_2009_%C3%9Cr%C3%BCmqi_riots&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Other organisations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<ul>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Amnesty_International" title="Amnesty International">Amnesty International</a></b>: called for an "impartial and independent" inquiry into the incident, adding that those detained for "peacefully expressing their views and exercising their freedom of expression, association and assembly" must be released and others ensured to receive a fair trial.<sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">[191]</a></sup></li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Human_Rights_Watch" title="Human Rights Watch">Human Rights Watch</a></b>: urged China to exercise restraint and to allow an independent inquiry into the events, which would include addressing Uyghur concerns about policies in the region. It also added that China should respect international norms when responding to the protests and only use force proportionately.<sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">[192]</a></sup></li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Al-Qaeda_in_the_Islamic_Maghreb" title="Al-Qaeda in the Islamic Maghreb">Al-Qaeda in the Islamic Maghreb (AQIM)</a></b>: According to London-based risk analysis firm Stirling Assynt, <a href="/wiki/Algeria" title="Algeria">Algeria</a>-based AQIM issued a call to attack Chinese workers in North Africa.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC-AQIM_193-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC-AQIM-193">[193]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">[194]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195">[195]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media_coverage">Media coverage</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=July_2009_%C3%9Cr%C3%BCmqi_riots&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Media coverage">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Chen Shirong, China editor on the <a href="/wiki/BBC_World_Service" title="BBC World Service">BBC World Service</a>, remarked at the improvement in media management by <a href="/wiki/Xinhua" class="mw-redirect" title="Xinhua">Xinhua</a>: "To be more credible, it released video footage a few hours after the event, not two weeks."<sup id="cite_ref-bbc090706_196-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc090706-196">[196]</a></sup> Peter Foster of the <i><a href="/wiki/Daily_Telegraph" class="mw-redirect" title="Daily Telegraph">Daily Telegraph</a></i> observed that "long-standing China commentators have been astonished at the speed at which Beijing has moved to seize the news agenda on this event," and attributed it to his belief that "China doesn't have a great deal to hide".<sup id="cite_ref-pfteleg090707_126-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pfteleg090707-126">[126]</a></sup> A University of California, Berkeley academic agreed that the Chinese authorities had become more sophisticated.<sup id="cite_ref-nyt090708_125-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nyt090708-125">[125]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i> and <a href="/wiki/Agence_France-Presse" title="Agence France-Presse">AFP</a> recognised the Chinese learnt lessons from political protests around the world, such as the so-called colour revolutions in <a href="/wiki/Rose_Revolution" title="Rose Revolution">Georgia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Orange_Revolution" title="Orange Revolution">Ukraine</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/2009_Iranian_election_protests" class="mw-redirect" title="2009 Iranian election protests">2009 Iranian election protests</a>, and concluded that Chinese experts had studied how modern electronic communications "helped protesters organize and reach the outside world, and for ways that governments sought to counter them."<sup id="cite_ref-nyt090708_125-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nyt090708-125">[125]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-AFP1_197-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AFP1-197">[197]</a></sup></p>
<p>But Willy Lam, fellow of <a href="/wiki/The_Jamestown_Foundation" class="mw-redirect" title="The Jamestown Foundation">the Jamestown Foundation</a>, sceptically said that the authorities were "just testing the reaction". He believed that if the outcome of this openness was poor they would "put the brakes on" as they did after the <a href="/wiki/2008_Sichuan_earthquake" title="2008 Sichuan earthquake">2008 Sichuan earthquake</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-AFP1_197-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AFP1-197">[197]</a></sup> There were instances of foreign journalists being taken into custody by the police, to be released shortly thereafter.<sup id="cite_ref-afraidtoevenlook_67-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-afraidtoevenlook-67">[67]</a></sup> On 10 July, officials ordered foreign media out of Kashgar, "for their own safety."<sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198">[198]</a></sup> Xia Lin, a top official at Xinhua, later revealed that violence caused by both sides during and after the riots had been downplayed or wholly unreported in official news channels, for the fear that the ethnic violence would spread beyond Ürümqi.<sup id="cite_ref-nyt20100603_199-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nyt20100603-199">[199]</a></sup></p>
<p>A <i>People's Daily</i> op-ed rebuked certain western media outlets for their "double standards, biased coverage and comments". It said that China failed to receive fair "repayment" from certain foreign political figures or media outlets for its openness and transparent attitude. The author said "a considerable number of media outlets still intentionally or inadvertently minimised the violent actions of the rioters, and attempted to focus on so-called racial conflict."<sup id="cite_ref-cnw20090710_200-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cnw20090710-200">[200]</a></sup> However, D'Arcy Doran from <i><a href="/wiki/Agence_France-Presse" title="Agence France-Presse">Agence France-Presse</a></i> welcomed the increased openness for foreign media, but contrasted their reporting to Chinese media, which closely followed the government line to focus mainly on injured Hans whilst ignoring the "Uyghur story" or reasons behind the incident.<sup id="cite_ref-AFP1_197-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AFP1-197">[197]</a></sup></p>
<p>Many early reports of the riots, starting with one from <a href="/wiki/Reuters" title="Reuters">Reuters</a>, used a picture purporting to show the previous day's riots.<sup id="cite_ref-SCMPphotogaffe_201-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SCMPphotogaffe-201">[201]</a></sup> The photo, showing large number of <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Armed_Police" title="People's Armed Police">People's Armed Police</a> squares, was one taken of the <a href="/wiki/2009_Shishou_riot" class="mw-redirect" title="2009 Shishou riot">2009 Shishou riot</a> and originally published on 26 June by <i>Southern Metropolis Weekly</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">[202]</a></sup> The same picture was mistakenly used by other agencies;<sup id="cite_ref-jaz090713_203-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jaz090713-203">[203]</a></sup> it was on the website of <i>The Daily Telegraph</i>, but was removed a day later.<sup id="cite_ref-SCMPphotogaffe_201-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SCMPphotogaffe-201">[201]</a></sup> In an interview with Al Jazeera on 7 July, WUC leader Rebiya Kadeer used the same Shishou photograph to defend the Uyghurs in Ürümqi.<sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204">[204]</a></sup> A World Uyghur Congress representative later apologised, explaining that the photo was chosen out of hundreds for its image quality.<sup id="cite_ref-jaz090713_203-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jaz090713-203">[203]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 3 August, Xinhua reported that two of Rebiya Kadeer's children had written letters blaming her for orchestrating the riots.<sup id="cite_ref-205" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-205">[205]</a></sup> A Germany-based spokesman for the WUC rejected the letters as fakes. A <a href="/wiki/Human_Rights_Watch" title="Human Rights Watch">Human Rights Watch</a> researcher remarked their style was "suspiciously close" to the way the Chinese authorities had described rioting in Xinjiang and the aftermath. He added that "it's highly irregular for [her children] to be placed on the platform of a government mouthpiece [...] for wide dispersion."<sup id="cite_ref-206" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-206">[206]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Aftermath_and_long-term_impact">Aftermath and long-term impact</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=July_2009_%C3%9Cr%C3%BCmqi_riots&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Aftermath and long-term impact">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Arrests_and_trials">Arrests and trials</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=July_2009_%C3%9Cr%C3%BCmqi_riots&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Arrests and trials">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Vertical_Banner_Urumqi.jpg" class="image"><img alt="A vertical, red banner hanging high on a building with Chinese writing: &quot;维护法律尊严，严惩犯罪分子&quot;" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Vertical_Banner_Urumqi.jpg/220px-Vertical_Banner_Urumqi.jpg" width="220" height="330" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Vertical_Banner_Urumqi.jpg/330px-Vertical_Banner_Urumqi.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Vertical_Banner_Urumqi.jpg/440px-Vertical_Banner_Urumqi.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="1500" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Vertical_Banner_Urumqi.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A red vertical banner saying "Uphold the sanctity of the law, and severely punish the criminals"</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In early August, the Ürümqi government announced that 83 individuals had been "officially" arrested in connection with the riots.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC83willbecharged_207-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC83willbecharged-207">[207]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-GTtrial_208-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GTtrial-208">[208]</a></sup> <i>China Daily</i> reported in late August that over 200 people were being charged and that trials would begin by the end of August.<sup id="cite_ref-BBCtrials_209-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBCtrials-209">[209]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-CNNtrials_210-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CNNtrials-210">[210]</a></sup> Although this was denied both by a provincial<sup id="cite_ref-GTtrial_208-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GTtrial-208">[208]</a></sup> and a local Party official,<sup id="cite_ref-NYTtrials_4-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYTtrials-4">[4]</a></sup> Xinjiang authorities later announced that arrest warrants had been issued to 196 suspects, of which 51 had already been prosecuted. Police also requested that the procuratorate approve the arrest of a further 239 people, and detention of 825 more, <i>China Daily</i> said.<sup id="cite_ref-211" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-211">[211]</a></sup> In early December, 94 "fugitives" were arrested.<sup id="cite_ref-bbcfugitives_212-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbcfugitives-212">[212]</a></sup></p>
<p>The state first announced criminal charges against detainees in late September, when it charged 21 people with "murder, arson, robbery, and damaging property".<sup id="cite_ref-21charged_213-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21charged-213">[213]</a></sup> 14,000 security personnel were deployed in Ürümqi from 11 October, and the next day a Xinjiang court sentenced six men to death, and one to life imprisonment,<sup id="cite_ref-XHsixdeath_214-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-XHsixdeath-214">[214]</a></sup> for their roles in the riots. All six men were Uyghurs, and were found guilty of murder, arson and robbery during the riots. Foreign media said the sentences appeared to be aimed at mollifying the anger of the Han majority;<sup id="cite_ref-guardian20091012_215-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardian20091012-215">[215]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-216" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-216">[216]</a></sup> the WUC denounced the verdict as "political", and said there was no desire to see justice served.<sup id="cite_ref-guardian20091012_215-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardian20091012-215">[215]</a></sup> Human Rights Watch said that there were "serious violations of due process" at the trials of 21 defendants relating to July protests. It said the trials "did not meet minimum international standards of due process and fair trials" – specifically, it said that the trials were carried out in a single day without prior public notice, that the defendants' choice of lawyers was restricted, and that the Party had given judges instructions on how to handle the cases.<sup id="cite_ref-HRW20091015_217-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HRW20091015-217">[217]</a></sup> Xinhua, on the other hand, noted that the proceedings were conducted in both the Chinese and Uyghur languages, and that evidence had been carefully collected and verified before any decisions were made.<sup id="cite_ref-XHsixdeath_214-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-XHsixdeath-214">[214]</a></sup></p>
<p>By February 2010, the number of death sentences issued had increased to at least 26,<sup id="cite_ref-26sentences_22-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26sentences-22">[22]</a></sup> including at least one Han and one female Uyghur.<sup id="cite_ref-riotwoman_20-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-riotwoman-20">[20]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-AP3sentence_218-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AP3sentence-218">[218]</a></sup> Nine of the individuals sentenced were executed in November 2009; based on previous government statements, eight were Uyghur and one was Han.<sup id="cite_ref-bbcnov_21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbcnov-21">[21]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-219" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-219">[219]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Later_unrest_and_security_measures">Later unrest and security measures</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=July_2009_%C3%9Cr%C3%BCmqi_riots&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Later unrest and security measures">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/September_2009_Xinjiang_unrest" title="September 2009 Xinjiang unrest">September 2009 Xinjiang unrest</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Armed_Police_armored_vehicles_in_Urumqi_(3).jpg" class="image"><img alt="A caravan of white armoured personnel carriers rolling through a city street, with soldiers carrying body shields marching alongside. Several civilians are standing by on the sidewalk." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Armed_Police_armored_vehicles_in_Urumqi_%283%29.jpg/220px-Armed_Police_armored_vehicles_in_Urumqi_%283%29.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Armed_Police_armored_vehicles_in_Urumqi_%283%29.jpg/330px-Armed_Police_armored_vehicles_in_Urumqi_%283%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Armed_Police_armored_vehicles_in_Urumqi_%283%29.jpg/440px-Armed_Police_armored_vehicles_in_Urumqi_%283%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="750" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Armed_Police_armored_vehicles_in_Urumqi_(3).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/People%27s_Armed_Police" title="People's Armed Police">Armed police</a> troops in <a href="/wiki/%C3%9Cr%C3%BCmqi" title="Ürümqi">Ürümqi</a> in early September 2009, after wide-scale civilian demonstrations and protests against the syringe attacks</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Starting in mid-August, there was a string of attacks in which as many as 476 individuals may have been stabbed with <a href="/wiki/Hypodermic_needle" title="Hypodermic needle">hypodermic needles</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-needlesquietsdown_220-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-needlesquietsdown-220">[220]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Bodeenneedles_221-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bodeenneedles-221">[221]</a></sup> Officials believed that the attacks were targeting Han civilians and had been perpetrated by Uyghur separatists.<sup id="cite_ref-BBCneedles_222-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBCneedles-222">[222]</a></sup> In response to both concern over the attacks<sup id="cite_ref-RFAnewriots_223-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RFAnewriots-223">[223]</a></sup> and dissatisfaction over the government's slowness in prosecuting people involved with the July riots, thousands of Hans protested in the streets.<sup id="cite_ref-APneedles_224-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-APneedles-224">[224]</a></sup> On 3 September, five people died during the protests and 14 were injured, according to an official.<sup id="cite_ref-tensionshighafter_225-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tensionshighafter-225">[225]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BBC5die_226-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC5die-226">[226]</a></sup> The next day, the Communist Party Chief of Ürümqi, <a href="/wiki/Li_Zhi_(official)" class="mw-redirect" title="Li Zhi (official)">Li Zhi</a>, was removed from his post, along with the police chief, Liu Yaohua;<sup id="cite_ref-227" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-227">[227]</a></sup> the provincial Party secretary <a href="/wiki/Wang_Lequan" title="Wang Lequan">Wang Lequan</a> was replaced in April 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-Wang_replaced_228-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wang_replaced-228">[228]</a></sup></p>
<p>While the city became calmer after these events, and the government made great efforts to show that life was returning to normal, an armed police presence did remain. As late as January 2010, it was reported that police were making patrols five or six times a day, and that patrols were stepped up at night.<sup id="cite_ref-shadows_19-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-shadows-19">[19]</a></sup> Shortly before the first anniversary of the rioting, the authorities installed more than 40,000 <a href="/wiki/Closed-circuit_television" title="Closed-circuit television">surveillance cameras</a> around Ürümqi to "ensure security in key public places".<sup id="cite_ref-apfcamera_229-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-apfcamera-229">[229]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Legislation_and_investigation">Legislation and investigation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=July_2009_%C3%9Cr%C3%BCmqi_riots&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Legislation and investigation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In late August, the central government passed a law outlining standards for the deployment of armed police during "rebellion, riots, large-scale serious criminal violence, terror attacks and other social safety incidents."<sup id="cite_ref-NYTnewlaw_230-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYTnewlaw-230">[230]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-SecurityManagement_231-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SecurityManagement-231">[231]</a></sup> After the protests in early September, the government issued an announcement banning all "unlicensed marches, demonstrations and mass protests".<sup id="cite_ref-banunlicensed_232-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-banunlicensed-232">[232]</a></sup> The provincial government also passed legislation banning the use of the internet to incite ethnic separatism.<sup id="cite_ref-MissingLink_119-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MissingLink-119">[119]</a></sup></p>
<p>In November, the Chinese government dispatched some 400 officials to Xinjiang, including senior leaders such as State Council secretary general <a href="/wiki/Ma_Kai" title="Ma Kai">Ma Kai</a>, Propaganda department head <a href="/wiki/Liu_Yunshan" title="Liu Yunshan">Liu Yunshan</a>, and <a href="/wiki/United_Front_(China)" class="mw-redirect" title="United Front (China)">United Front</a> chief <a href="/wiki/Du_Qinglin" title="Du Qinglin">Du Qinglin</a>, to form an ad hoc "Team of Investigation and Research" on Xinjiang, ostensibly intended on studying the policy changes to be implemented in response to the violence.<sup id="cite_ref-Liyuhui_233-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Liyuhui-233">[233]</a></sup> In April 2010, hardliner party chief <a href="/wiki/Wang_Lequan" title="Wang Lequan">Wang Lequan</a> was replaced by <a href="/wiki/Zhang_Chunxian" title="Zhang Chunxian">Zhang Chunxian</a>, a more conciliatory figure.<sup id="cite_ref-nytaj_234-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nytaj-234">[234]</a></sup> The government authorized transfer payments totalling some $15 billion from eastern provinces to Xinjiang to aid in the province's economic development, and announced plans to establish a <a href="/wiki/Special_economic_zone" title="Special economic zone">special economic zone</a> in <a href="/wiki/Kashgar" title="Kashgar">Kashgar</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-nytaj_234-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nytaj-234">[234]</a></sup></p>
<p>China has installed a grassroots network of officials throughout Xinjiang, its predominantly Muslim north-west frontier region, to address social risks and spot early signs of unrest: Hundreds of cadres have been transferred from southern Xinjiang, the region’s poorest area, into socially unstable neighbourhoods of Ürümqi; a policy has been implemented where if all family members are unemployed, the government arranges for one person in the household to get a job,; official announcements are calling upon university students to register for those payouts. The areas around slums are being redeveloped to reduce social risks, opening way to new apartment blocks.<sup id="cite_ref-235" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-235">[235]</a></sup> However, independent observers believe that fundamental inequalities need to be addressed, and the mindset must change for there to be any success; Ilham Tohti warned that the new policy could attract more Han immigration, and further alienate the Uyghur population.<sup id="cite_ref-236" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-236">[236]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Public_services_and_Internet_access">Public services and Internet access</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=July_2009_%C3%9Cr%C3%BCmqi_riots&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Public services and Internet access">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>It took until at least early August for public transport to be fully restored in the city. According to Xinhua, 267 buses had been damaged during the rioting;<sup id="cite_ref-Xinhuabuscomp_237-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Xinhuabuscomp-237">[237]</a></sup> most were back in operation by 12 August.<sup id="cite_ref-Xinhuabuses_238-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Xinhuabuses-238">[238]</a></sup> The government paid bus companies a total of ¥5.25&#160;million in compensation.<sup id="cite_ref-Xinhuabuscomp_237-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Xinhuabuscomp-237">[237]</a></sup> Despite the resumption of transportation services, and the government's efforts to encourage visitors to the region, tourism fell sharply after the riots;<sup id="cite_ref-shadows_19-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-shadows-19">[19]</a></sup> on the <a href="/wiki/National_Day_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China" title="National Day of the People's Republic of China">National Day</a> holiday in October, Xinjiang had 25% fewer tourists than it did in 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-tourismslump_239-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tourismslump-239">[239]</a></sup></p>
<p>Ürümqi public schools opened on schedule in September for the fall semester, but with armed police guarding them. Many schools began first-day classes by focusing on patriotism.<sup id="cite_ref-schoolopening_240-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-schoolopening-240">[240]</a></sup></p>
<p>On the other hand, Internet and international telephone service in Ürümqi remained limited for nearly a year after the riots. As late as November, most of the Internet was still inaccessible to residents and international phone calls were impossible;<sup id="cite_ref-MissingLink_119-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MissingLink-119">[119]</a></sup> as late as December, most web content hosted outside the autonomous region remained off-limits to all but a few journalists,<sup id="cite_ref-TeaguevideoInternet_241-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TeaguevideoInternet-241">[241]</a></sup> and residents had to travel to <a href="/wiki/Dunhuang" title="Dunhuang">Dunhuang</a> 14 hours away to access the Internet normally. Within the city, only about 100 local sites, such as banks and regional government websites, could be accessed.<sup id="cite_ref-MissingLink_119-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MissingLink-119">[119]</a></sup> Both incoming and outgoing international phone calls were disallowed, so Ürümqi residents could only communicate by calling intermediaries in other cities in China who would then place the international calls.<sup id="cite_ref-MissingLink_119-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MissingLink-119">[119]</a></sup> The communications blackout generated controversy even within China: Yu Xiaofeng of <a href="/wiki/Zhejiang_University" title="Zhejiang University">Zhejiang University</a> criticised the move, and many Ürümqi locals said it hurt businesses and delayed recovery, whereas David Gosset of the Euro-China forum argued that the government had the right to shut down communications for the sake of social stability; some locals believed that getting away from the Internet even improved their quality of life.<sup id="cite_ref-MissingLink_119-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MissingLink-119">[119]</a></sup></p>
<p>In late December, the government began restoring services gradually. The websites for Xinhua and the <i>People's Daily</i>, two state-controlled media outlets, were made accessible on 28 December, the web portals <a href="/wiki/Sina.com" class="mw-redirect" title="Sina.com">Sina.com</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sohu.com" class="mw-redirect" title="Sohu.com">Sohu.com</a> on 10 January 2010,<sup id="cite_ref-XHtexting_242-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-XHtexting-242">[242]</a></sup> and 27 more websites on 6 February.<sup id="cite_ref-CuiJiawebsites_243-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CuiJiawebsites-243">[243]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-CDmorwebsites_244-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CDmorwebsites-244">[244]</a></sup> But access to websites was only partial: for instance, users could browse forums and blogs but not post on them.<sup id="cite_ref-CuiJiawebsites_243-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CuiJiawebsites-243">[243]</a></sup> <i>China Daily</i> reported that limited e-mail services were also restored in Ürümqi on 8 February, although a BBC reporter writing at approximately the same time said e-mail was not accessible yet.<sup id="cite_ref-trekking_245-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-trekking-245">[245]</a></sup> Text messaging on cell phones was restored on 17 January, although there was a limit to how many messages a user could send daily.<sup id="cite_ref-XHtextrestored_246-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-XHtextrestored-246">[246]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BBCtextrestored_247-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBCtextrestored-247">[247]</a></sup> Internet access was fully restored in May 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-InternetRestored_120-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-InternetRestored-120">[120]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=July_2009_%C3%9Cr%C3%BCmqi_riots&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: References">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<li id="cite_note-5"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-5">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The riots are also referred to as the <b>Urumqi 5 July Incident</b> (<a href="/wiki/Simplified_Chinese_characters" title="Simplified Chinese characters">simplified Chinese</a>: <span lang="zh-Hans">乌鲁木齐7·5事件</span>; <a href="/wiki/Traditional_Chinese_characters" title="Traditional Chinese characters">traditional Chinese</a>: <span lang="zh-Hant">烏魯木齊7·5事件</span>), or even simply as <b>5 July Incident</b>. State media and government officials refer to it as <i>Ürümqi 7·5 Rioting Serious Violent Criminal Incident</i> (<a href="/wiki/Simplified_Chinese_characters" title="Simplified Chinese characters">simplified Chinese</a>: <span lang="zh-Hans">乌鲁木齐“7·5”打砸抢烧严重暴力犯罪事件</span>; <a href="/wiki/Traditional_Chinese_characters" title="Traditional Chinese characters">traditional Chinese</a>: <span lang="zh-Hant">烏魯木齊「7·5」打砸搶燒嚴重暴力犯罪事件</span>).</span></li>

<li id="cite_note-csm-74"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-csm_74-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation news">Marquand, Robert (12 July 2009). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.csmonitor.com/2009/0712/p06s07-wogn.html">"Q&amp;A with Uighur spiritual leader Rebiya Kadeer"</a>. <i>Christian Science Monitor</i><span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">18 January</span> 2010</span>. <q>[Kadeer:] I was quite surprised by the loss of so many lives. Initially the protest was peaceful. You could even see Uighurs in the crowd holding Chinese flags. There were women and children, and that seemed at first like a good thing. But the Uighurs were provoked by Chinese security forces – dogs, armoured cars. What has not been noted are the plain clothes police who went in and provoked the Uighurs. My view is that the Chinese wanted a riot in order to justify a larger crackdown; it's an attempt to create solidarity between the Han and the government at a time when there is insecurity. Provoking the crowd justifies that this was a Uighur mob.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AJuly+2009+%C3%9Cr%C3%BCmqi+riots&amp;rft.atitle=Q%26A+with+Uighur+spiritual+leader+Rebiya+Kadeer&amp;rft.aufirst=Robert&amp;rft.aulast=Marquand&amp;rft.date=2009-07-12&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.csmonitor.com%2F2009%2F0712%2Fp06s07-wogn.html&amp;rft.jtitle=Christian+Science+Monitor&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal" class="Z3988"><span style="display:none;">&#160;</span></span></span></li>
